            <p>The <i>b</i> values are derived from the slope of linear graphs in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202403736-fig-0009">9b</a>, with values of 0.99 for cathodic peaks and 1.0 for anodic peaks. The <i>b</i>-values indicate that pseudocapacitive effects primarily influence the reversible Na-ion deintercalation/intercalation process. In addition, we can theoretically determine the pseudocapacitive and diffusion-controlled contributions using the equation <i>i</i>  = <i>k</i><sub>1</sub> <i>v</i> + <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>, as stated in equation <a class="equationLink scrollableLink" href="#smll202403736-disp-0008" title="Link to equation">8</a>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202403736-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202403736-bib-0060_R_d89545366e2360" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Nano Res.">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202403736-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/80a5a9e1-1949-4d47-9e5d-25ac17784a70/smll202403736-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/80a5a9e1-1949-4d47-9e5d-25ac17784a70/smll202403736-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/14811108-a143-4087-b4fe-b0d3b59a844b/smll202403736-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/80a5a9e1-1949-4d47-9e5d-25ac17784a70/smll202403736-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 9<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202403736-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202403736" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves at six sweep rates, b) plots of log (peak current) versus log (scan rate) at different redox states, c) relative contribution of the capacitive and diffusion-controlled charge storage at different scan rates for Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC, d) GITT curves of Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC anode at Na-ion battery (The inset curves show the calculated Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients of Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC during the discharge–charge processes at 0.1 Ag<sup>−1</sup>).</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202403736-fig-0009">9c</a> shows that the pseudocapacitive contribution is determined to be 79%, 84%, 88%, 90%, 91%, and 92% for scan speeds of 0.1, 0.2, 0.4, 0.6, 0.8, and 1.0 mVs<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. As the scan rate increases, the capacitive contribution becomes increasingly noticeable and eventually reaches 92% at a scan rate of 1.0 mVs<sup>−1</sup>. The findings unequivocally demonstrate that the pseudocapacitive charge storage constitutes a significant component of the overall capacity, particularly at elevated scan speeds.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202403736-bib-0068" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202403736-bib-0068_R_d89545366e2418" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 68 - ACS Nano">68</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The enhanced rate performance and long-term cycle stability may be ascribed to a substantial portion of capacitance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202403736-bib-0066" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202403736-bib-0066_R_d89545366e2424" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 66 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">66</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">In order to investigate the sodium-ion storage processes of Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC throughout the discharge/charge process, we used a Galvanostatic Intermittent Titration Technique (GITT) to quantify the sodium-ion diffusion coefficient. The diffusion coefficients (D<sub>Na+</sub>) in Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC were determined using the following formula.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202403736-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202403736-bib-0062_R_d89545366e2446" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - Rare Met.">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="smll202403736-disp-0009"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                     <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/a863d8eb-77d1-46d3-89bc-9f704c3a316d/smll202403736-math-0009.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16136810:media:smll202403736:smll202403736-math-0009" display="block" location="graphic/smll202403736-math-0009.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <mrow>
                              <mi>D</mi>
                              <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                              <mfrac>
                                 <mn>4</mn>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <mi>π</mi>
                                    <mi>τ</mi>
                                 </mrow>
                              </mfrac>
                              <msup>
                                 <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                                    <mfrac>

                                          <msub>

                                          <msub>
                                             <mi>V</mi>
                                             <mi>M</mi>
                                          </msub>
                                       </mrow>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi>S</mi>

                                       </mrow>

                              </msup>
                              <mo>·</mo>

                                 <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                                    <mfrac>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi>
                                          <msub>

                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}D = \frac{4}{{\pi \tau }} {\left( {\frac{{{m_B}{V_M}}}{{S{M_B}}}} \right)^2} \cdot {\left( {\frac{{{{\Delta}}{E_s}}}{{{{\Delta}}{E_t}}}} \right)^2}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(10)</span></div><i>m<sub>B</sub></i> and <i>V<sub>M</sub></i> represent the molar number and molar volume of the sample, respectively, while τ denotes the time of pulse current. <i>S</i> denotes the region of the electrode that is capable of producing a desired effect. Δ<i>E<sub>s</sub></i> and Δ<i>E</i><sub>τ</sub> represent the disparity between two equilibrium potentials and the disparity between the potentials before and after the pulse, respectively. For Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC anode material, the calculated average D<sub>Na+</sub> (1.16&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−10</sup>–3.35&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−9</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>−1</sup>) and D<sub>Li+</sub> (1.62&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−11</sup>–2.25&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−9</sup> cm<sup>2</sup>s<sup>−1</sup>) values were observed from Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). The anode composed of Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC exhibits a larger D<sub>Na+</sub> value compared to the D<sub>Li+</sub> cell during both the discharge and charge processes (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). This suggests that Na<sup>+</sup> ions have a greater tendency to diffuse in Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC, which is in line with the findings of the theoretical simulation.</div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">In situ, X-ray diffraction (XRD) was conducted to investigate the phase transformation in the Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC electrode throughout the process of sodiationdesodiation and to determine the composition of the charge–discharge products. In the in situ XRD patterns (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#smll202403736-fig-0010">10a</a>), the diffraction peaks at 45.6° (100), 50.7° (002), and 52.6° (101) correspond to the Be (COD no 9012015) from the test device. During discharge, we noted the expected decrease in intensity of the peak at 33.47° (002) associated with the Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> crystal plane (COD no. 9012804). The special diffraction peaks of Cu<sub>2</sub>Se (26.65° (111)) progressively shift toward lower angles and decrease in intensity as a result of the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> ions throughout the discharge process. In contrast, when the discharge voltage drops below 0.8&nbsp;V, the distinct peaks of Na<sub>2</sub>Se at 22.5° (111) start to become visible. The Cu and Co peaks are indiscernible because low-crystallinity copper/cobalt may have formed, which was not detected by XRD. Based on the transformation mechanism of the Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC anode in a Na-ion battery, it is observed that the formation of Na<sub>2</sub>Se also leads to the formation of Cu and Co. As the battery charges, the peaks of Na<sub>2</sub>Se progressively fade away,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202403736-bib-0066" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202403736-bib-0066_R_d89545366e2608" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 66 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">66</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and some of the created Cu<sub>2</sub>Se may be recognized in the contour plots of in situ XRD. The peaks of Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> did not exhibit an apparent presence through the charging process, probably due to the formation of an amorphous Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub> phase. The illustration for the conversion mechanism of Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202403736-fig-0010">10b</a>. The reduction and oxidation peaks seen in the in situ XRD data and mentioned in the literature<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#smll202403736-bib-0070" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202403736-bib-0070_R_d89545366e2634" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 70 - Nano Energy">70</a>, <a href="#smll202403736-bib-0071" class="bibLink tab-link" id="smll202403736-bib-0071_R_d89545366e2634" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 71 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">71</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> can be attributed to the following electrochemical reactions:

            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="smll202403736-fig-0010"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/d627d576-a297-4359-8efc-18d44cca8087/smll202403736-fig-0010-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/d627d576-a297-4359-8efc-18d44cca8087/smll202403736-fig-0010-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/254aa100-71c2-45ae-8d18-c08888f4a35f/smll202403736-fig-0010-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/d627d576-a297-4359-8efc-18d44cca8087/smll202403736-fig-0010-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 10<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=smll202403736-fig-0010&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fsmll.202403736" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">In situ XRD patterns of Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC and corresponding GCD curves during the initial one cycle at 100 mAg<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>Comparing the data from LiBs and SIBs measurements with similar electrode materials in existing literature reveals that the obtained results surpass several electrode materials in terms of capacity and stability. Comparing the performance of electrode materials derived from ZIF-12 with those of LiBs and SIBs, it is evident that the electrode material obtained is significantly superior in LiBs. Until yet, there have been no reports on the performance of any electrode material made from ZIF-12 in SIBs. Based on these findings, it is evident that the developed electrode material is highly advantageous for both LIBs and SIBs and has the potential to significantly contribute to research in this area.</p>
            </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="smll202403736-sec-0060">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="smll202403736-sec-0060-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In brief, we effectively produced Co@NPC, Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC, and Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC composites by subjecting ZIF-12 and Cu@ZIF-12 precursors to calcination. Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC composites exhibit improved stability and conductivity. The composite construction has various benefits, including reducing volume expansion, enhancing the rates of Li<sup>+</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> insertion, and improving long-term cycling performance. The Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC material exhibits a reversible capacity of 543 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> after undergoing 750 cycles at a current density of 2 Ag<sup>−1</sup> in Li-ion batteries. Similarly, in Na-ion batteries, the material retains a reversible capacity of 185 mAhg<sup>−1</sup> after undergoing 1000 cycles at a current density of 2 Ag<sup>−1</sup>.</p>
         
         <p>TheCE maintains nearly 99% for Li-ion (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202403736-fig-0005">5d</a>) and 100% for Na-ion (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#smll202403736-fig-0008">8e</a>) cells in the long cycling process. The in situ XRD measurements provided confirmed the lithium/sodium storage mechanism of Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC. Furthermore, the role of pseudocapacitance is completely validated using CV testing. The pseudocapacitance contribution rates for Li-ion and Na-ion cells are 80% and 92%, respectively, at a scanning speed of 1 mVs<sup>−1</sup>. This study aims to further the investigation of using carbon-hosted bimetallic composites obtained from ZIF-12 as highly effective electrode material both LIBs and SIBs. In addition, the Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup> storage capabilities of the optimized Cu<sub>2</sub>Se/Co<sub>3</sub>Se<sub>4</sub>@NPC are comparable to that of other metal selenide anode materials described in recent research (Tables <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
